       51 +## Grounding cascade (3 priority tiers)                       
       52 +`ground_scene()` tries in order:                              
       53 +1. **Dataset annotations** ‚ÄĒ if `annotations` arg is provided 
       54 +2. **HSV segmentation** ‚ÄĒ `ground_scene_hsv()`; detects colore
          +d blocks; min area 400px¬≤, max 12 objects                     
       55 +3. **VLM grounding** ‚ÄĒ Claude API call; only if `USE_VLM_FOR_G
          +ROUNDING=True` and API key set                                
       56  
       57 +## Image coordinate scaling                                   
       58 +`main.py` downscales images with long edge > 1280px (to keep V
          +LM payload < 5MB), tracks `(scale_x, scale_y)`,               
       59 +then rescales grounded bboxes/centers back to original coordin
          +ates for final output via `scale_objects()`.                  
       60 +All pipeline internals (trajectories, goal_pixel, bboxes) oper
          +ate in **downscaled space**.                                  
       61 +                                                              
       62  ## Key component contracts
       48 -- `ground_scene(image, annotations=None)` ‚Üí list of `{name, bb
          -ox, center, confidence}`

          -ment_specification` field

          - or None

          -CE_NOT_FOUND,

          -INSUFFICIENT_GOAL_SPECIFICATION

          -t of validated trajectory dicts

          -valid/rejected tracking)

          -ulationResult

> update spec.md to handle multiple objects : Handling Multiple Matching        
  Objects                                                                       
                                                                                
  The system shall handle scenes containing multiple objects of the same type.  
                                                                                
  Examples:                                                                     
                                                                                
  two cups                                                                      
  three bottles                                                                 
  multiple books                                                                
  two red blocks                                                                
  several objects matching the word "mug"                                       
                                                                                
  The Object Grounding stage shall assign a unique object_id to every detected  
  object.                                                                       
                                                                                
  Example:                                                                      
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "object_id": "cup_1",                                                         
  "name": "cup",                                                                
  "bbox": [x1, y1, x2, y2],                                                     
  "center": [x, y],                                                             
  "attributes": ["white"],                                                      
  "spatial_description": "left cup"                                             
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "object_id": "cup_2",                                                         
  "name": "cup",                                                                
  "bbox": [x1, y1, x2, y2],                                                     
  "center": [x, y],                                                             
  "attributes": ["blue"],                                                       
  "spatial_description": "right cup"                                            
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  Disambiguation Using Prompt Descriptors                                       
                                                                                
  The LLM Goal Interpreter Agent shall extract disambiguating descriptors from  
  the prompt when available.                                                    
                                                                                
  Descriptors may include:                                                      
                                                                                
  color: red cup, blue bottle                                                   
  location: left cup, right cup, top bowl, bottom book                          
  relation: cup near laptop, bottle beside plate                                
  size: small box, large bowl                                                   
  ordinal: first cup, second bottle                                             
  region: cup on left side of table, book near edge                             
                                                                                
  Example:                                                                      
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  move the left cup near the laptop                                             
                                                                                
  Structured goal:                                                              
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "target_object": "cup",                                                       
  "target_descriptors": ["left"],                                               
  "reference_object": "laptop",                                                 
  "spatial_relation": "near"                                                    
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  The grounding resolver shall use target_object plus target_descriptors to     
  select the correct object instance.                                           
                                                                                
  Ambiguity Interrupt                                                           
                                                                                
  If multiple objects match the target object and the prompt does not contain   
  sufficient descriptors to select one unique object, the system shall raise an 
  interrupt before trajectory generation.                                       
                                                                                
  Example:                                                                      
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  move the cup near the laptop                                                  
                                                                                
  Scene:                                                                        
                                                                                
  two cups visible                                                              
                                                                                
  Interrupt:                                                                    
                                                                                
  Multiple cups are visible. Please specify which cup, for example: left cup,   
  right cup, blue cup, or cup near the plate.                                   
                                                                                
  When ambiguity occurs:                                                        
                                                                                
  do not generate candidate trajectories                                        
  do not call VLM trajectory reasoning                                          
  do not run VLMPC validation                                                   
  log all matching object candidates                                            
  ask the user for clarification                                                
  Reference Object Ambiguity                                                    
                                                                                
  The same rule applies to reference objects.                                   
                                                                                
  Example:                                                                      
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  move the mug beside the book                                                  
                                                                                
  Scene:                                                                        
                                                                                
  one mug, three books                                                          
                                                                                
  Interrupt:                                                                    
                                                                                
  Multiple books are visible. Please specify which book, for example: left      
  book, right book, top book, or book near the laptop.                          
                                                                                
  Grounding Resolver Output                                                     
                                                                                
  The grounding resolver shall output:                                          
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "status": "resolved" | "ambiguous" | "not_found",                             
  "selected_object_id": "cup_1" | null,                                         
  "candidate_object_ids": ["cup_1", "cup_2"],                                   
  "reason": "descriptor matched left cup"                                       
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  Evaluation Tests                                                              
                                                                                
  Add tests for duplicate-object scenes.                                        
                                                                                
  Add:                                                                          
                                                                                
  evaluation/tests/test_object_disambiguation.py                                
                                                                                
  Test cases:                                                                   
                                                                                
  Scene has two cups, prompt says "move the left cup near laptop"               
  Expected: resolves left cup                                                   
  Scene has two cups, prompt says "move the blue cup near laptop"               
  Expected: resolves blue cup                                                   
  Scene has two cups, prompt says "move the cup near laptop"                    
  Expected: ambiguity interrupt                                                 
  Scene has one mug and three books, prompt says "move mug beside book"         
  Expected: reference object ambiguity interrupt                                
  Scene has multiple red blocks, prompt says "move red block near blue block"   
  Expected: ambiguity interrupt unless one red block is uniquely grounded by    
  additional relation                                                           
  Scene has two bottles, prompt says "move bottle closest to plate away from    
  plate"                                                                        
  Expected: resolves bottle closest to plate

      147  
      148  #### 4.1.2 Output Schema
      149  
      150 +Each detected object shall be assigned a unique `object_id` co
          +mposed of its name and a 1-based index suffix (e.g. `cup_1`, `
          +cup_2`). Objects that appear only once in the scene use suffix
          + `_1`.                                                        
      151 +                                                              
      152  ```json
      153  {
      154 +  "object_id": "cup_1",                                       
      155    "name": "cup",
      156    "bbox": [x1, y1, x2, y2],
      157    "center": [x, y],
      158    "confidence": 0.91,
      156 -  "source": "dataset"                                         
      159 +  "source": "dataset",                                        
      160 +  "attributes": ["white"],                                    
      161 +  "spatial_description": "left cup"                           
      162  }
      163  ```
      164  
      165  `source` values: `"dataset"` | `"hsv"` | `"vlm"`
      166  
      167 +`attributes`: color, size, or other visually observable proper
          +ties extracted by the grounding step. May be empty (`[]`).    
      168 +                                                              
      169 +`spatial_description`: a short human-readable locator derived 
          +from the object's position relative to other scene objects (e.
          +g. `"left cup"`, `"top book"`, `"cup near laptop"`). Generated
          + by the grounder for disambiguation display in interrupt messa
          +ges.                                                          
      170 +                                                              
      171  Consumers: LLM Goal Interpreter, Interrupt Validation, PIVOT G
           enerator, Collision Validator, Clearance Analyzer.
      172  
      173 +#### 4.1.3 Grounding Resolver                                 
      174 +                                                              
      175 +After `ground_scene()` returns the object list, the **Groundin
          +g Resolver** selects the specific object instance referenced b
          +y the structured goal. It is called once for the target object
          + and once for the reference object (if present).              
      176 +                                                              
      177 +**Input:** `object_list`, `target_name`, `target_descriptors` 
      178 +                                                              
      179 +**Resolution logic (in order):**                              
      180 +                                                              
      181 +1. Filter objects by `name` matching `target_name`.           
      182 +2. If exactly one match ‚Üí resolved.                           
      183 +3. If zero matches ‚Üí `not_found`.                             
      184 +4. If multiple matches, apply `target_descriptors` (color, spa
          +tial location, relation, size, ordinal) to narrow to one match
          +.                                                             
      185 +5. If descriptors narrow to exactly one ‚Üí resolved.           
      186 +6. If descriptors still leave multiple matches or no descripto
          +rs are present ‚Üí `ambiguous`.                                 
      187 +                                                              
      188 +**Output schema:**                                            
      189 +                                                              
      190 +```json                                                       
      191 +{                                                             
      192 +  "status": "resolved" | "ambiguous" | "not_found",           
      193 +  "selected_object_id": "cup_1",                              
      194 +  "candidate_object_ids": ["cup_1", "cup_2"],                 
      195 +  "reason": "descriptor matched left cup"                     
      196 +}                                                             
      197 +```                                                           
      198 +                                                              
      199 +`selected_object_id` is `null` when `status` is `"ambiguous"` 
          +or `"not_found"`.                                             
      200 +                                                              
      201  ### 4.2 LLM Goal Interpreter Agent
      202  
      203  Converts a natural-language prompt and the detected objects li
           st into a structured planning goal.

      463  
      464 +#### 4.3.3 Object Ambiguity Interrupt                         
      465 +                                                              
      466 +The `TARGET_AMBIGUOUS` interrupt is raised when the Grounding 
          +Resolver returns `status == "ambiguous"` for the target object
          + ‚ÄĒ i.e. multiple scene objects match `target_object` and the a
          +vailable `target_descriptors` are insufficient to select exact
          +ly one.                                                       
      467 +                                                              
      468 +The `REFERENCE_AMBIGUOUS` interrupt is raised under the same c
          +ondition for the reference object.                            
      469 +                                                              
      470 +**When ambiguity occurs:**                                    
      471 +- Do not generate candidate trajectories.                     
      472 +- Do not call VLM trajectory reasoning.                       
      473 +- Do not run VLMPC validation.                                
      474 +- Log all `candidate_object_ids` in `log.json`.               
      475 +- Display a clarification message naming the candidates and su
          +ggesting how to disambiguate.                                 
      476 +                                                              
      477 +**Example ‚ÄĒ target ambiguity:**                               
      478 +                                                              
      479 +Scene: two cups visible. Prompt: `"move the cup near the lapto
          +p"`                                                           
      480 +                                                              
      481 +```                                                           
      482 +Multiple cups are visible. Please specify which cup, for examp
          +le:                                                           
      483 +  left cup, right cup, blue cup, or cup near the plate.       
      484 +```                                                           
      485 +                                                              
      486 +**Example ‚ÄĒ reference ambiguity:**                            
      487 +                                                              
      488 +Scene: one mug, three books. Prompt: `"move the mug beside the
          + book"`                                                       
      489 +                                                              
      490 +```                                                           
      491 +Multiple books are visible. Please specify which book, for exa
          +mple:                                                         
      492 +  left book, right book, top book, or book near the laptop.   
      493 +```                                                           
      494 +                                                              
      495 +The clarification message shall list the `spatial_description`
          + of each candidate object (from ¬ß4.1.2) to help the user ident
          +ify them.                                                     
      496 +                                                              
      497  On any interrupt: trajectory generation stops, simulation does
            not run, interrupt reason and code are written to `log.json`,
            message is displayed on console and in any web UI.

> further update spec.md to handle destination ambiguity, removal corner cases  
  : Destination Object Disambiguation and Removal Goal Handling                 
                                                                                
  The object disambiguation logic shall apply to both the target object and the 
  destination/reference object.                                                 
                                                                                
  Example:                                                                      
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  place the mug to the left of the glass                                        
                                                                                
  Scene:                                                                        
                                                                                
  one mug and three glasses                                                     
                                                                                
  The system shall not only fail with a generic ambiguity message. It shall     
  explain the reason clearly:                                                   
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "status": "interrupt",                                                        
  "reason": "ambiguous_reference_object",                                       
  "message": "Multiple glasses were identified in the image. Please specify     
  which glass, for example: left glass, right glass, glass near plate, or blue  
  glass.",                                                                      
  "candidate_reference_objects": ["glass_1", "glass_2", "glass_3"]              
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  If the prompt contains enough descriptors to resolve the                      
  destination/reference object, the system shall continue.                      
                                                                                
  Examples:                                                                     
                                                                                
  place mug to left of the right glass                                          
  place mug beside the glass near the plate                                     
  place mug near the blue glass                                                 
                                                                                
  The grounding resolver shall log both target-object and reference-object      
  ambiguity separately.                                                         
                                                                                
  Removal Commands with Source Region                                           
                                                                                
  The system shall support removal-style prompts of the form:                   
                                                                                
  remove glass from table                                                       
  remove glass from background                                                  
  remove glass from carpet                                                      
  clear cup from desk                                                           
  take bottle away from shelf                                                   
  remove object from workspace                                                  
                                                                                
  For removal commands, the phrase after "from" shall be treated as a source    
  region or contextual region.                                                  
                                                                                
  The source region does not need to be detected as a physical object.          
                                                                                
  Examples:                                                                     
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  remove glass from table                                                       
                                                                                
  If "table" is not detected:                                                   
                                                                                
  The system shall not fail only because the source region was not detected.    
                                                                                
  Instead, it shall continue planning and log a warning:                        
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "warning": "source_region_not_grounded",                                      
  "source_region": "table",                                                     
  "message": "The source region 'table' was not detected as an object.          
  Proceeding with removal trajectory using visible image/workspace boundary."   
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  remove glass from background                                                  
                                                                                
  If "background" is not detected:                                              
                                                                                
  Continue planning and log:                                                    
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "warning": "source_region_not_grounded",                                      
  "source_region": "background",                                                
  "message": "The source region 'background' was treated as contextual scene    
  region. Proceeding with removal trajectory."                                  
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  For removal commands:                                                         
                                                                                
  target object must still be grounded                                          
  source region may remain ungrounded                                           
  ungrounded source region shall be recorded as warning, not failure            
  trajectory planning shall continue if target object is valid                  
                                                                                
  The system shall fail only if the target object is missing or ambiguous, or   
  if no safe removal trajectory can be found.                                   
                                                                                
  Edge, End, and Corner Goals                                                   
                                                                                
  The system shall support prompts referring to scene boundaries or surface     
  boundaries.                                                                   
                                                                                
  Examples:                                                                     
                                                                                
  move cup to edge of table                                                     
  move glass to end of floor                                                    
  move book to corner of carpet                                                 
  remove cup to edge                                                            
  move object to nearest edge                                                   
  clear object from table                                                       
                                                                                
  If the named surface such as table, floor, or carpet is not explicitly        
  detected, the system shall approximate the goal using image-space boundaries  
  or visible workspace boundaries.                                              
                                                                                
  The system shall not fail only because the surface object is not grounded.    
                                                                                
  It shall log a warning:                                                       
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "warning": "surface_region_not_grounded",                                     
  "surface_region": "table",                                                    
  "message": "Surface region 'table' was not detected. Using image/workspace    
  boundary approximation."                                                      
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  For edge/end/corner goals, the planner shall evaluate candidate trajectories  
  toward image or workspace boundaries.                                         
                                                                                
  The selected trajectory shall be:                                             
                                                                                
  shortest feasible path to a valid boundary or corner region                   
  inside image bounds unless explicitly exiting workspace                       
  collision-free                                                                
  maximum possible clearance among feasible short paths                         
  logged with closest object distance and minimum clearance                     
                                                                                
  Examples:                                                                     
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  move cup to edge of table                                                     
                                                                                
  If table boundary is detected:                                                
                                                                                
  Plan toward nearest feasible table edge.                                      
                                                                                
  If table boundary is not detected:                                            
                                                                                
  Plan toward nearest feasible image/workspace edge and log warning.            
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  move book to corner of carpet                                                 
                                                                                
  If carpet is not detected:                                                    
                                                                                
  Plan toward nearest feasible image corner or workspace corner and log         
  warning.                                                                      
                                                                                
  Boundary Goal Candidate Generation                                            
                                                                                
  For boundary-style goals, the PIVOT Candidate Generator shall generate        
  candidate paths toward:                                                       
                                                                                
  nearest left edge                                                             
  nearest right edge                                                            
  nearest top edge                                                              
  nearest bottom edge                                                           
  nearest corner, if corner is requested                                        
                                                                                
  The planner shall evaluate candidates and select the safest feasible path.    
                                                                                
  For each candidate, compute:                                                  
                                                                                
  path length                                                                   
  collision status                                                              
  closest object                                                                
  minimum clearance                                                             
  boundary distance                                                             
  final distance to selected edge/corner                                        
                                                                                
  The final selected path shall minimize:                                       
                                                                                
  collision risk                                                                
  path length                                                                   
  final distance to edge/corner                                                 
                                                                                
  while maintaining required clearance.                                         
                                                                                
  Updated Interrupt Policy                                                      
                                                                                
  The system shall interrupt when:                                              
                                                                                
  target object is missing                                                      
  target object is ambiguous                                                    
  reference object is ambiguous for placement tasks                             
  goal is incomplete                                                            
  no safe trajectory exists                                                     
                                                                                
  The system shall not interrupt when:                                          
                                                                                
  source region after "from" is not detected in a removal command               
  surface name in "edge of table", "corner of carpet", or "end of floor" is not 
  detected                                                                      
                                                                                
  In these cases, continue with image/workspace boundary approximation and log

      498 +                                                              
      499 +```json                                                       
      500 +{                                                             
      501 +  "status": "interrupt",                                      
      502 +  "code": "REFERENCE_AMBIGUOUS",

          +lease specify which glass, for example: left glass, right glas
          +s, glass near plate, or blue glass.",                         
      505 +  "candidate_reference_objects": ["glass_1", "glass_2", "glass
          +_3"]                                                          
      506 +}                                                             
      507 +```                                                           
      508 +                                                              
      509 +If the prompt contains sufficient descriptors to resolve the r
          +eference object, the system shall continue without interruptin
          +g. Examples that resolve:                                     
      510 +                                                              
      511 +```                                                           
      512 +place mug to left of the right glass       ‚Üí reference_descrip
          +tors: ["right"]

          +tors: ["near plate"]                                          
      514 +place mug near the blue glass              ‚Üí reference_descrip
          +tors: ["blue"]                                                
      515 +```                                                           
      516 +                                                              
      517 +The Grounding Resolver (¬ß4.1.3) is applied independently to bo
          +th target and reference objects. Each produces its own `status
          +` / `selected_object_id` / `candidate_object_ids`. Both resolu
          +tions are logged under `target_resolution` and `reference_reso
          +lution` in `log.json`.                                        
      518 +                                                              
      519 +#### 4.3.4 Interrupt Policy Summary                           
      520 +                                                              
      521 +The system shall interrupt only for conditions that make plann
          +ing impossible or unsafe:                                     
      522 +                                                              
      523 +| Condition | Interrupts? | Code |                            
      524 +|---|---|---|                                                 
      525 +| Target object not found in scene | Yes | `TARGET_NOT_FOUND` 
          +|                                                             
      526 +| Target object ambiguous (no descriptors resolve it) | Yes | 
          +`TARGET_AMBIGUOUS` |                                          
      527 +| Reference object ambiguous (placement/spatial tasks) | Yes |
          + `REFERENCE_AMBIGUOUS` |                                      
      528 +| Goal direction/type uninterpretable | Yes | `GOAL_UNINTERPRE
          +TABLE` |                                                      
      529 +| Movement underspecified (no distance, coords, or reference) 
          +| Yes | `INSUFFICIENT_GOAL_SPECIFICATION` |                   
      530 +| Removal destination entirely unclear | Yes | `REMOVAL_DESTIN
          +ATION_UNCLEAR` |                                              
      531 +| Source region after "from" not detected as object | **No** ‚ÄĒ
          + log warning, continue |                                      
      532 +| Surface name in "edge of table" / "corner of carpet" not det
          +ected | **No** ‚ÄĒ log warning, continue |                      
      533 +| No safe trajectory exists after simulation | Yes | `NO_FEASI
          +BLE_TRAJECTORY` |                                             
      534 +                                                              
      535 +#### 4.3.5 Ungrounded Source and Surface Regions              
      536 +                                                              
      537 +For **removal commands** (`remove X from Y`, `clear X from Y`,
          + `take X away from Y`), the phrase after "from" is treated as 
          +a source region. Source regions do not need to be detected as 
          +physical objects.                                             
      538 +                                                              
      539 +If the source region is not grounded, the system shall:       
      540 +- Continue with trajectory planning using image/workspace boun
          +dary as exit target.                                          
      541 +- Log a warning (not an interrupt):                           
      542 +                                                              
      543 +```json                                                       
      544 +{                                                             
      545 +  "warning": "source_region_not_grounded",                    
      546 +  "source_region": "table",                                   
      547 +  "message": "The source region 'table' was not detected as an
          + object. Proceeding with removal trajectory using visible imag
          +e/workspace boundary."                                        
      548 +}                                                             
      549 +```                                                           
      550 +                                                              
      551 +For **boundary/edge/corner goals** (`move cup to edge of table
          +`, `move book to corner of carpet`, `move glass to end of floo
          +r`), the named surface does not need to be detected.          
      552 +                                                              
      553 +If the surface is not grounded, the system shall:             
      554 +- Continue with trajectory planning toward the nearest feasibl
          +e image/workspace boundary.                                   
      555 +- Log a warning:                                              
      556 +                                                              
      557 +```json                                                       
      558 +{                                                             
      559 +  "warning": "surface_region_not_grounded",                   
      560 +  "surface_region": "table",                                  
      561 +  "message": "Surface region 'table' was not detected. Using i
          +mage/workspace boundary approximation."                       
      562 +}                                                             
      563 +```                                                           
      564 +                                                              
      565 +Warnings are written to `log.json` under `"warnings": []` and 
          +displayed in the web UI. They do not halt the pipeline.       
      566 +                                                              
      567  On any interrupt: trajectory generation stops, simulation does
            not run, interrupt reason and code are written to `log.json`,
            message is displayed on console and in any web UI.

      630  
      631  `points_scaled` = processing-resolution coordinates. `points_o
           riginal` = original-resolution coordinates (see ¬ß4.9). `goal_p
           ixel` = the computed target point used to orient this trajecto
           ry.
      632  
      633 +#### 4.4.5 Boundary Goal Candidate Generation                 
      634 +                                                              
      635 +For goal types that target a scene boundary (`remove_from_surf
          +ace`, edge/end/corner goals), the generator shall produce cand
          +idate trajectories toward each of the four image edges (left, 
          +right, top, bottom) plus the four corners when a corner goal i
          +s requested.                                                  
      636 +                                                              
      637 +**Target point computation for boundary goals:**              
      638 +                                                              
      639 +| Goal phrase | Candidate target points |                     
      640 +|---|---|                                                     
      641 +| `edge of <surface>` / `to edge` | Nearest point on each of t
          +he 4 image edges from the target object center |              
      642 +| `end of <surface>` | Same as edge |                         
      643 +| `corner of <surface>` / `to corner` | 4 image corner points 
          +|                                                             
      644 +| `remove X from Y` (surface ungrounded) | Nearest point on ea
          +ch image edge |                                               
      645 +                                                              
      646 +The generator produces one candidate per direction (up to `NUM
          +_CANDIDATES`); if fewer boundary targets exist than `NUM_CANDI
          +DATES`, the remaining slots are filled by fan-angle variation 
          +around the dominant boundary direction.                       
      647 +                                                              
      648 +**Per-candidate boundary metrics** (added to trajectory dict):
      649 +                                                              
      650 +```json                                                       
      651 +{                                                             
      652 +  "boundary_target": "left_edge",                             
      653 +  "boundary_distance": 12.4                                   
      654 +}                                                             
      655 +```                                                           
      656 +                                                              
      657 +`boundary_distance` = Euclidean distance from trajectory endpo
          +int to the target edge/corner point.                          
      658 +                                                              
      659 +**Selection criteria for boundary goals (¬ß4.9 validator, bound
          +ary mode):**                                                  
      660 +                                                              
      661 +1. No collision                                               
      662 +2. Minimum clearance ‚Č• 10px                                   
      663 +3. Shortest `boundary_distance`                               
      664 +4. Shorter path length                                        
      665 +5. Lowest total cost                                          
      666 +

           ning.

‚úĽ Brewed for 2m 52s

> update spec.md for multiple objects in prompt : Quantity-Aware Object         
  Selection                                                                     
                                                                                
  The LLM Goal Interpreter Agent shall extract quantity information from the    
  prompt.                                                                       
                                                                                
  Examples:                                                                     
                                                                                
  move one screw                                                                
  remove a screw                                                                
  move two bottles                                                              
  clear three cups from table                                                   
  place one mug beside laptop                                                   
                                                                                
  Structured goal:                                                              
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "target_object": "screw",                                                     
  "quantity": 1                                                                 
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  or                                                                            
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "target_object": "cup",                                                       
  "quantity": 3                                                                 
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  If quantity is omitted, default:                                              
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "quantity": "all_matching"                                                    
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  unless the prompt semantics indicate a singular object.                       
                                                                                
  Automatic Candidate Selection                                                 
                                                                                
  When multiple instances of the target object exist and the requested quantity 
  is less than the number of matching objects, the system shall automatically   
  evaluate candidate objects instead of immediately raising an ambiguity        
  interrupt.                                                                    
                                                                                
  Example:                                                                      
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  remove one screw from table                                                   
                                                                                
  Scene:                                                                        
                                                                                
  screw_1                                                                       
  screw_2                                                                       
  screw_3                                                                       
                                                                                
  The planner shall:                                                            
                                                                                
  generate candidate trajectories for each screw                                
  evaluate collision risk                                                       
  evaluate clearance                                                            
  evaluate path length                                                          
  evaluate distance to goal region                                              
  select the best candidate                                                     
                                                                                
  The selected object shall be the object with the lowest planning cost.        
                                                                                
  Planning Cost Function                                                        
                                                                                
  The candidate ranking shall consider:                                         
                                                                                
  collision-free status                                                         
  minimum clearance                                                             
  trajectory length                                                             
  distance to requested goal region                                             
  distance to image/workspace boundary when applicable                          
                                                                                
  The exact weighting may evolve during development.                            
                                                                                
  Quantity-Based Selection Examples                                             
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  remove one screw from table                                                   
                                                                                
  Behavior:                                                                     
                                                                                
  Select the screw that yields the safest and shortest valid removal            
  trajectory.                                                                   
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  move one bottle to the left of the laptop                                     
                                                                                
  Behavior:                                                                     
                                                                                
  Evaluate all bottles.                                                         
                                                                                
  Select the bottle that yields the safest valid trajectory satisfying the      
  goal.                                                                         
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  place one mug beside the plate                                                
                                                                                
  Behavior:                                                                     
                                                                                
  Evaluate all mugs.                                                            
                                                                                
  Select the mug producing the best valid placement trajectory.                 
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  move two screws near the motor                                                
                                                                                
  Behavior:                                                                     
                                                                                
  Rank all screws.                                                              
                                                                                
  Select the two highest-ranked candidates.                                     
                                                                                
  When to Raise Ambiguity Interrupt                                             
                                                                                
  An ambiguity interrupt shall only occur when:                                 
                                                                                
  multiple candidate objects exist                                              
  quantity information is insufficient                                          
  multiple candidates have equivalent planning scores                           
  the planner cannot confidently select a preferred candidate                   
                                                                                
  Example:                                                                      
                                                                                
  Prompt:                                                                       
                                                                                
  move the screw beside the motor                                               
                                                                                
  Scene:                                                                        
                                                                                
  five screws with similar trajectory costs                                     
                                                                                
  Result:                                                                       
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "status": "interrupt",                                                        
  "reason": "multiple_equally_valid_candidates",                                
  "candidate_objects": [                                                        
  "screw_1",                                                                    
  "screw_2",                                                                    
  "screw_3",                                                                    
  "screw_4",                                                                    
  "screw_5"                                                                     
  ]                                                                             
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  Reference Object Handling                                                     
                                                                                
  Destination and reference objects shall continue to require unique            
  resolution.                                                                   
                                                                                
  Example:                                                                      
                                                                                
  place mug left of glass                                                       
                                                                                
  Scene:                                                                        
                                                                                
  three glasses                                                                 
                                                                                
  Result:                                                                       
                                                                                
  interrupt                                                                     
                                                                                
  Reason:                                                                       
                                                                                
  multiple destination objects identified.                                      
                                                                                
  The interrupt shall list candidate destination objects.                       
                                                                                
  The system shall not automatically choose a destination object unless the     
  prompt explicitly specifies quantity or descriptors.                          
                                                                                
  Trace Logging                                                                 
                                                                                
  Log:                                                                          
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
  "candidate_objects": [...],                                                   
  "quantity_requested": 1,                                                      
  "candidate_scores": [...],                                                    
  "selected_objects": [...],

  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  The trace shall explain why a particular object instance was selected.

      705  4. Shorter path length
      706  5. Lowest total cost
      707  
      708 +#### 4.4.6 Multi-Object Candidate Evaluation                  
      709 +                                                              
      710 +When `quantity` is an integer and multiple matching objects ex
          +ist, the generator runs the full trajectory generation and sim
          +ulation pipeline for each candidate object instance, then sele
          +cts the best `quantity` instances.                            
      711 +                                                              
      712 +**Process:**                                                  
      713 +                                                              
      714 +1. Identify all objects matching `target_object` (from groundi
          +ng output).                                                   
      715 +2. For each candidate object, generate `NUM_CANDIDATES` trajec
          +tories using that object's center as the start point.         
      716 +3. Simulate all trajectories (¬ß4.7).                          
      717 +4. Compute per-object best-trajectory cost (lowest cost among 
          +that object's candidates).                                    
      718 +5. Rank objects by their best-trajectory cost using the priori
          +ty order: collision-free ‚Üí clearance ‚Üí path length ‚Üí distance 
          +to goal region ‚Üí total cost.                                  
      719 +6. Select the top `quantity` ranked objects. For each selected
          + object, the trajectory with the lowest cost is used.         
      720 +                                                              
      721 +**Tie-breaking tolerance:** if the top two candidates have cos
          +ts within 5% of each other (`abs(cost_a - cost_b) / max(cost_a
          +, cost_b) < 0.05`), they are considered equal and `TARGET_AMBI
          +GUOUS` (`multiple_equally_valid_candidates`) is raised (¬ß4.3.3
          + Case 3).                                                     
      722 +                                                              
      723 +**Trace logging per multi-object run:**                       
      724 +                                                              
      725 +```json                                                       
      726 +{                                                             
      727 +  "candidate_objects": ["screw_1", "screw_2", "screw_3"],     
      728 +  "quantity_requested": 1,                                    
      729 +  "candidate_scores": [                                       
      730 +    {"object_id": "screw_1", "best_cost": 45.2, "collision": f
          +alse, "clearance": 32.1},                                     
      731 +    {"object_id": "screw_2", "best_cost": 78.9, "collision": f
          +alse, "clearance": 18.4},                                     
      732 +    {"object_id": "screw_3", "best_cost": 210.0, "collision": 
          +true,  "clearance": 0.0}                                      
      733 +  ],                                                          
      734 +  "selected_objects": ["screw_1"],                            
      735 +  "selection_reason": "lowest planning cost"                  
      736 +}                                                             
      737 +```                                                           
      738 +

‚óŹ Now I have a complete picture. Let me compare the spec additions against all
  six implementation files systematically.

  ---
  Gap Analysis ‚ÄĒ New Spec vs. Current Implementation

  ¬ß4.1.2 ‚ÄĒ Grounding output schema (grounder.py)

  Spec requires: object_id (e.g. cup_1), attributes: [], spatial_description on
  every grounded object.

  Current: All three paths (dataset, HSV, VLM) return only {name, bbox, center, 
  confidence, source}.

  Gap: object_id, attributes, spatial_description are entirely absent from
  grounder output.

  ---
  ¬ß4.1.3 ‚ÄĒ Grounding Resolver (grounder.py)

  Spec requires: A resolve_object(object_list, target_name, target_descriptors)
  function returning {status, selected_object_id, candidate_object_ids, reason}.

  Current: Does not exist. interrupt.py has a bare _matching_objects() helper
  but no descriptor-based resolution.

  Gap: Grounding Resolver is completely missing.

  ---
  ¬ß4.2.1 / ¬ß4.2.4 ‚ÄĒ target_descriptors, reference_descriptors, quantity 
  (interpreter.py)

  Spec requires: Three new fields in structured goal output; quantity extracted
  from "one screw", "two bottles", "a cup" etc.

  Current: Neither the offline parser nor the VLM prompt extract or return any
  of these fields. The VLM prompt schema listed in _parse_vlm also doesn't
  mention them.

  Gap: All three fields missing from both parse paths. VLM prompt will also need
  updating.

  ---
  ¬ß4.3.3 ‚ÄĒ Quantity-aware ambiguity logic (interrupt.py)

  Spec requires:
  - quantity integer + multiple matches ‚Üí auto-select by cost, no interrupt
  - quantity == "all_matching" + unresolvable ‚Üí TARGET_AMBIGUOUS
  - quantity == 1 + all costs tied ‚Üí TARGET_AMBIGUOUS
  (multiple_equally_valid_candidates)

  Current: interrupt.py line 84‚Äď88 ‚ÄĒ len(target_matches) > 1 always raises
  TARGET_AMBIGUOUS regardless of quantity. There is no cost evaluation at
  interrupt time.

  Gap: The entire quantity-aware branch doesn't exist. This is the most
  significant behavioral gap ‚ÄĒ prompts like "remove one screw" will always
  interrupt instead of auto-selecting.

  ---
  ¬ß4.3.4 ‚ÄĒ Descriptor-based reference resolution (interrupt.py)

  Spec requires: Apply reference_descriptors from structured goal to narrow
  multiple reference matches before raising REFERENCE_AMBIGUOUS.

  Current: Line 112‚Äď116 ‚ÄĒ len(ref_matches) > 1 always raises
  REFERENCE_AMBIGUOUS. No descriptor narrowing.

  Gap: Descriptor resolution absent for reference objects.

  ---
  ¬ß4.3.5 ‚ÄĒ Ungrounded source/surface region warnings (interrupt.py)

  Spec requires: If source region after "from" isn't a grounded object ‚Üí log
  warning, continue. Same for surface names in edge/corner goals.

  Current: _SURFACE_REGIONS set (lines 96‚Äď102) already skips interrupt for known
  surface words in removal tasks. So the "don't interrupt" part works ‚ÄĒ but no
  warning is logged, and source_region_grounded / warnings fields are never
  populated.

  Gap: Partial ‚ÄĒ interrupt is correctly skipped, but warning logging and
  log.json fields are missing.

  ---
  ¬ß4.4.5 ‚ÄĒ Boundary goal candidate generation (generator.py)

  Spec requires: For edge/corner goals, generate candidates toward all 4 edges
  (or 4 corners); add boundary_target and boundary_distance to each trajectory
  dict.

  Current: _compute_goal_pixel picks a single nearest-boundary point for
  remove_from_surface goals. No boundary_target/boundary_distance fields on
  trajectory dicts, no multi-direction fan toward different edges.

  Gap: Single-direction only; trajectory fields missing; no
  edge_goal/corner_goal goal_type handling.

  ---
  ¬ß4.4.6 ‚ÄĒ Multi-object candidate evaluation (generator.py / main.py)

  Spec requires: When quantity is integer, loop over all matching objects, run
  full trajectory+simulation for each, rank by cost, select top N.

  Current: generate_candidates() takes a fixed start point from the first
  matching object. No multi-object loop exists anywhere.

  Gap: Entirely missing. This requires orchestration across generator.py,
  rollout.py, and a new ranking step that currently has no home.

  ---
  ¬ß4.13 ‚ÄĒ log.json new fields (logger.py / main.py)

  Spec requires: target_resolution, reference_resolution, source_region,
  source_region_grounded, surface_region, surface_region_grounded, warnings,
  candidate_objects, quantity_requested, candidate_scores, selected_objects,
  selection_reason.

  Current: logger.py is a pass-through ‚ÄĒ it serialises whatever data dict is
  passed. None of these fields are being populated by the pipeline in main.py.

  Gap: All new fields absent from pipeline output.

  ---

      114 +def _spatial_description(obj, all_objects):                   
      115 +    """                                                       
      116 +    Derive a short human-readable locator for obj relative to 
          +peers of the same name.                                       
      117 +    E.g. "left cup", "top book". Falls back to the object name
          + alone.                                                       
      118 +    """                                                       
      119 +    name = obj["name"]                                        
      120 +    peers = [o for o in all_objects if o["name"] == name]     
      121 +    if len(peers) <= 1:                                       
      122 +        return name                                           
      123 +                                                              
      124 +    cx, cy = obj["center"]                                    
      125 +    peer_centers_x = sorted(set(o["center"][0] for o in peers)
          +)                                                             
      126 +    peer_centers_y = sorted(set(o["center"][1] for o in peers)
          +)                                                             
      127 +                                                              
      128 +    # Use left/right or top/bottom depending on which axis has
          + more spread                                                  
      129 +    x_span = peer_centers_x[-1] - peer_centers_x[0] if len(pee
          +r_centers_x) > 1 else 0                                       
      130 +    y_span = peer_centers_y[-1] - peer_centers_y[0] if len(pee
          +r_centers_y) > 1 else 0                                       
      131 +                                                              
      132 +    if x_span >= y_span:                                      
      133 +        idx = peer_centers_x.index(cx)                        
      134 +        labels = ["left", "center", "right"] if len(peer_cente
          +rs_x) == 3 else (                                             
      135 +            ["left", "right"] if len(peer_centers_x) == 2 else
      136 +            [f"pos{i+1}" for i in range(len(peer_centers_x))] 
      137 +        )                                                     
      138 +        label = labels[min(idx, len(labels) - 1)]             
      139 +    else:                                                     
      140 +        idx = peer_centers_y.index(cy)                        
      141 +        labels = ["top", "center", "bottom"] if len(peer_cente
          +rs_y) == 3 else (                                             
      142 +            ["top", "bottom"] if len(peer_centers_y) == 2 else
      143 +            [f"pos{i+1}" for i in range(len(peer_centers_y))] 
      144 +        )                                                     
      145 +        label = labels[min(idx, len(labels) - 1)]             
      146 +                                                              
      147 +    return f"{label} {name}"                                  
      148 +                                                              
      149 +                                                              
      150 +def _assign_ids_and_descriptions(objects):                    
      151 +    """                                                       
      152 +    Add object_id, attributes, spatial_description to each obj
          +ect in-place.                                                 
      153 +    object_id = name_slug + "_" + 1-based index among peers.  
      154 +    """                                                       
      155 +    from collections import defaultdict                       
      156 +    counts = defaultdict(int)                                 
      157 +    for obj in objects:                                       
      158 +        slug = re.sub(r"[^a-z0-9]+", "_", obj["name"].lower())
          +.strip("_")                                                   
      159 +        counts[slug] += 1                                     
      160 +        obj["object_id"] = f"{slug}_{counts[slug]}"           
      161 +        if "attributes" not in obj:                           
      162 +            # Extract color from HSV name (e.g. "red square" ‚Üí
          + ["red"])                                                     
      163 +            words = obj["name"].lower().split()               
      164 +            color_words = {"red", "blue", "green", "yellow", "
          +orange", "purple",                                            
      165 +                           "cyan", "white", "black", "gray", "
          +grey", "pink", "brown"}                                       
      166 +            obj["attributes"] = [w for w in words if w in colo
          +r_words]                                                      
      167 +                                                              
      168 +    # Assign spatial_description after all objects are known  
      169 +    for obj in objects:                                       
      170 +        obj["spatial_description"] = _spatial_description(obj,
          + objects)                                                     
      171 +                                                              
      172 +    return objects
