      418 +def resolve_object(objects, target_name, target_descriptors=No
          +ne):                                                          
      419 +    """                                                       
      420 +    Grounding Resolver per spec ¬ß4.1.3.                       
      421 +                                                              
      422 +    Selects a unique object from `objects` matching `target_na
          +me`, optionally                                               
      423 +    narrowed by `target_descriptors` (list of color/location/r
          +elation strings).                                             
      424 +                                                              
      425 +    Returns:                                                  
      426 +        {                                                     
      427 +            "status":              "resolved" | "ambiguous" | 
          +"not_found",                                                  
      428 +            "selected_object_id":  str | None,                
      429 +            "candidate_object_ids": list[str],                
      430 +            "reason":              str,                       
      431 +        }                                                     
      432 +    """                                                       
      433 +    target_descriptors = target_descriptors or []             
      434 +                                                              
      435 +    if not objects or not target_name:                        
      436 +        return {                                              
      437 +            "status": "not_found",                            
      438 +            "selected_object_id": None,                       
      439 +            "candidate_object_ids": [],                       
      440 +            "reason": "no objects or target name provided",   
      441 +        }                                                     
      442 +                                                              
      443 +    name_l = target_name.lower().strip()                      
      444 +    # Match by name substring (word-boundary first, then subst
          +ring)                                                         
      445 +    exact = [o for o in objects if name_l in o["name"].lower()
          +.split()]                                                     
      446 +    candidates = exact if exact else [o for o in objects if na
          +me_l in o["name"].lower()]                                    
      447 +                                                              
      448 +    candidate_ids = [o.get("object_id", o["name"]) for o in ca
          +ndidates]                                                     
      449 +                                                              
      450 +    if len(candidates) == 0:                                  
      451 +        return {                                              
      452 +            "status": "not_found",                            
      453 +            "selected_object_id": None,                       
      454 +            "candidate_object_ids": [],                       
      455 +            "reason": f"no object named '{target_name}' found 
          +in scene",                                                    
      456 +        }                                                     
      457 +                                                              
      458 +    if len(candidates) == 1:                                  
      459 +        return {                                              
      460 +            "status": "resolved",                             
      461 +            "selected_object_id": candidates[0].get("object_id
          +", candidates[0]["name"]),                                    
      462 +            "candidate_object_ids": candidate_ids,            
      463 +            "reason": "unique match",                         
      464 +        }                                                     
      465 +                                                              
      466 +    # Multiple candidates ‚ÄĒ apply descriptors to narrow       
      467 +    if target_descriptors:                                    
      468 +        narrowed = candidates                                 
      469 +        for desc in target_descriptors:                       
      470 +            desc_l = desc.lower().strip()                     
      471 +            filtered = [                                      
      472 +                o for o in narrowed                           
      473 +                if desc_l in (o.get("spatial_description") or 
          +"").lower()                                                   
      474 +                or any(desc_l in a.lower() for a in (o.get("at
          +tributes") or []))                                            
      475 +                or desc_l in o["name"].lower()                
      476 +            ]                                                 
      477 +            if filtered:                                      
      478 +                narrowed = filtered                           
      479 +                                                              
      480 +        if len(narrowed) == 1:                                
      481 +            return {                                          
      482 +                "status": "resolved",                         
      483 +                "selected_object_id": narrowed[0].get("object_
          +id", narrowed[0]["name"]),                                    
      484 +                "candidate_object_ids": candidate_ids,        
      485 +                "reason": f"descriptor matched {narrowed[0].ge
          +t('spatial_description', narrowed[0]['name'])}",              
      486 +            }                                                 
      487 +        if len(narrowed) == 0:                                
      488 +            # Descriptors over-constrained ‚ÄĒ fall through to a
          +mbiguous                                                      
      489 +            pass                                              
      490 +        else:                                                 
      491 +            candidates = narrowed                             
      492 +            candidate_ids = [o.get("object_id", o["name"]) for
          + o in candidates]                                             
      493 +                                                              
      494 +    return {                                                  
      495 +        "status": "ambiguous",                                
      496 +        "selected_object_id": None,                           
      497 +        "candidate_object_ids": candidate_ids,                
      498 +        "reason": f"{len(candidates)} candidates after descrip
          +tor filtering",                                               
      499 +    }                                                         
      500 +                                                              
      501 +

      503      """
      504      Return target pixel (x, y) where the goal should be achiev
           ed.

       70 +def _extract_quantity(goal_str):                              
       71 +    """                                                       
       72 +    Return (quantity, quantity_explicit).                     
       73 +    quantity: int | "all_matching"                            
       74 +    quantity_explicit: True when a number was stated in the pr
          +ompt.                                                         
       75 +    """                                                       
       76 +    m = _QUANTITY_RE.search(goal_str)                         
       77 +    if m:                                                     
       78 +        raw = m.group(1).lower()                              
       79 +        if raw.isdigit():                                     
       80 +            return int(raw), True                             
       81 +        if raw in _QUANTITY_WORDS:                            
       82 +            return _QUANTITY_WORDS[raw], True                 
       83 +    return "all_matching", False                              
       84 +                                                              
       85 +                                                              
       86 +# ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ Descriptor extraction ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
          +‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ                                            
       87 +                                                              
       88 +_COLOR_WORDS = {                                              
       89 +    "red", "blue", "green", "yellow", "orange", "purple",     
       90 +    "cyan", "white", "black", "gray", "grey", "pink", "brown",
       91 +}                                                             
       92 +_SIDE_WORDS = {"left", "right", "top", "bottom", "upper", "low
          +er", "front", "back"}                                         
       93 +_SIZE_WORDS = {"small", "large", "big", "tiny", "huge", "tall"
          +, "short", "wide"}                                            
       94 +_ORDINAL_WORDS = {"first", "second", "third", "fourth", "last"
          +}                                                             
       95 +                                                              
       96 +                                                              
       97 +def _extract_descriptors(fragment):                           
       98 +    """                                                       
       99 +    Extract disambiguating descriptors from a noun phrase frag
          +ment.                                                         
      100 +    Returns list of descriptor strings.                       
      101 +    """                                                       
      102 +    if not fragment:                                          
      103 +        return []                                             
      104 +    words = fragment.lower().split()                          
      105 +    descriptors = []                                          
      106 +    for w in words:                                           
      107 +        if w in _COLOR_WORDS or w in _SIDE_WORDS or w in _SIZE
          +_WORDS or w in _ORDINAL_WORDS:                                
      108 +            descriptors.append(w)                             
      109 +    return descriptors                                        
      110 +

‚óŹ 103 passed, 3 skipped.

  Root cause and fixes:

  Two bugs in _parse_offline for removal prompts:

  1. _REMOVE_CONTEXT was too narrow ‚ÄĒ it required "from the table" or "from a 
  table" but not bare "from table". Prompts like "remove glass from table",
  "remove one screw from table" fell through to the else branch, which set
  target_fragment = "one screw from table" (the entire remainder). Fixed by
  adding "from" and "away from" to the pattern, and extending the surface word
  list to include background, carpet, workspace, etc.
  2. Quantity words weren't stripped from target_fragment ‚ÄĒ even when the
  context matched, "one screw" would fail to find a match for "one screw" in the
  objects list. Fixed by stripping leading quantity words ("one screw" ‚Üí
  "screw") before the object lookup.

‚óŹ Good. Now I have the full trace picture. Let me identify all three issues
  precisely before writing the spec:

  Issue 1 ‚ÄĒ Grounding offset (apple/screw):
  - apple.jpg: VLM detects "peach" not "apple" ‚ÄĒ the prompt says "apple" but the
  grounder returns "peach". The _best_match function does substring matching so
  "apple" doesn't match "peach". The target ends up being the first-matched
  object by fallback. This is a VLM grounding accuracy + synonym/alias problem.
  - screws.jpg: Screws are detected fine but screw_1 at center [390,199] ‚ÄĒ the
  screw positions look reasonable but the "best" screw selected (screw_1) has
  goal_error=120.6 (never reaches the boundary). This is a boundary trajectory 
  not reaching edge problem.

  Issue 2 ‚ÄĒ Attribute-based object matching:
  - plliars.jpg: target_descriptors: ['blue'] is extracted but the
  resolve_object() function only matches on attributes and spatial_description
  fields ‚ÄĒ but the VLM grounder doesn't populate attributes from VLM output (it
  only extracts color from HSV name strings). So "blue" descriptor can't match
  against VLM-detected "pliers" objects.
  - lens_remote.jpg: VLM detects "TV remote", "Sony remote", "Panasonic remote"
  but target is "remote" ‚ÄĒ none match by substring because exact word "remote"
  is in all of them but the _best_match finds all three, and "big" descriptor
  can't narrow because attributes=[].

  Issue 3 ‚ÄĒ Boundary clearance:
  - clamp all waypoints to 5px inside image bounds is already in ¬ß4.4.2 but the
  border collision check in rollout uses border_margin=10. These need to be
  consistent and explicitly stated as a hard guarantee.

      230  
      231  `selected_object_id` is `null` when `status` is `"ambiguous"` 
           or `"not_found"`.
      232  
      233 +#### 4.1.4 Object Name Matching and Synonym Expansion         
      234 +                                                              
      235 +All object name comparisons throughout the pipeline (Grounding
          + Resolver, interrupt checker, generator origin lookup) shall u
          +se **tolerant matching**:                                     
      236 +                                                              
      237 +1. **Substring word match** ‚ÄĒ a prompt noun matches a grounded
          + object name if it appears as any whole word in the name. `"re
          +mote"` matches `"TV remote"`, `"Sony remote"`, `"Panasonic rem
          +ote"`.                                                        
      238 +2. **Substring match** ‚ÄĒ if word match yields nothing, fall ba
          +ck to substring. `"glass"` matches `"wine glass"`.            
      239 +3. **Attribute-based match** ‚ÄĒ if a prompt descriptor (color, 
          +size) appears in an object's `attributes` list, that object is
          + a candidate regardless of name. `"blue"` matches any object w
          +ith `attributes: ["blue", ...]`.                              
      240 +                                                              
      241 +**Common synonym groups** the grounder and resolver shall expa
          +nd:                                                           
      242 +                                                              
      243 +| Prompt word | Matches grounded names containing |           
      244 +|---|---|                                                     
      245 +| `apple` | `apple`, `red apple`, `green apple`, `fruit` |    
      246 +| `remote` | `remote`, `controller`, `TV remote`, `clicker` | 
      247 +| `pliers` | `pliers`, `plier`, `tool` |                      
      248 +| `glass` | `glass`, `cup`, `wine glass`, `drinking glass` |  
      249 +| `bottle` | `bottle`, `flask`, `jar` |                       
      250 +| `book` | `book`, `notebook`, `magazine` |                   
      251 +| `cup` | `cup`, `mug`, `glass`, `beaker` |                   
      252 +                                                              
      253 +Synonym expansion is applied as a fallback only ‚ÄĒ exact and su
          +bstring matches take priority. Custom synonyms may be added to
          + `config.py` under `OBJECT_SYNONYMS`.                         
      254 +                                                              
      255 +#### 4.1.5 Attribute-Based Object Selection                   
      256 +                                                              
      257 +When a prompt contains an attribute descriptor (color, size) t
          +hat the Grounding Resolver cannot match against `spatial_descr
          +iption`, the resolver shall also match against:               
      258 +                                                              
      259 +- `attributes` list (from VLM `color`/`size` fields, ¬ß4.1.1a) 
      260 +- words within the object `name` (e.g. `"blue pliers"` has `"b
          +lue"` in the name)                                            
      261 +                                                              
      262 +This enables prompts like `"move the blue pliers"`, `"pick up 
          +the big remote"`, `"remove the pink pliers"` to resolve correc
          +tly even when no `spatial_description` is available.          
      263 +                                                              
      264 +**Attribute matching fallback chain:**                        
      265 +                                                              
      266 +1. Exact attribute in `attributes` list ‚Üí candidate           
      267 +2. Attribute word appears in object `name` ‚Üí candidate        
      268 +3. Attribute word appears in `spatial_description` ‚Üí candidate
      269 +                                                              
      270 +If exactly one candidate remains after attribute filtering ‚Üí r
          +esolved. If multiple remain ‚Üí `ambiguous` (prompt the user for
          + further disambiguation). If none remain ‚Üí ignore attribute fi
          +lter and fall back to all name-matched candidates.            
      271 +                                                              
      272  ### 4.2 LLM Goal Interpreter Agent
      273  
      274  Converts a natural-language prompt and the detected objects li
           st into a structured planning goal.

      1584 +#### 13.12.1 Object Grounding Offset and Name Mismatch       
      1585 +                                                             
      1586 +**Observed:** `apple.jpg` ‚ÄĒ VLM grounder returned `"peach"` f
           +or objects that are visually apples. The prompt `"remove left
           + apple from table"` failed to match any grounded object becau
           +se `"apple"` ‚Č† `"peach"`.                                    
      1587 +                                                             
      1588 +**Root cause:** VLM uses its own naming conventions; prompt n
           +ouns may not match exactly.                                  
      1589 +                                                             
      1590 +**Fix:** ¬ß4.1.4 synonym expansion + tolerant substring matchi
           +ng. `"apple"` now matches `"red apple"`, `"fruit"`. VLM promp
           +t updated (¬ß4.1.1a) to use canonical common names and return 
           +`attributes` including `color`.

      1602 +                                                             
      1603 +**Observed:** `plliars.jpg` ‚ÄĒ prompt `"move the blue pliers"`
           + extracts `target_descriptors: ["blue"]` but `resolve_object(
           +)` cannot match `"blue"` against any pliers object because `a
           +ttributes: []` (VLM grounder does not populate attributes).  
      1604 +                                                             
      1605 +Similarly `lens_remote.jpg` ‚ÄĒ prompt `"move the big remote"` 
           +extracts `"big"` but VLM returns `"TV remote"`, `"Sony remote
           +"`, `"Panasonic remote"` all with `attributes: []`.          
      1606 +                                                             
      1607 +**Root cause:** `_assign_ids_and_descriptions()` only extract
           +s color from HSV-style names (e.g. `"red square"`); VLM-groun
           +ded objects get empty `attributes`.                          
      1608 +                                                             
      1609 +**Fix:** ¬ß4.1.1a ‚ÄĒ VLM prompt requests `color` and `size`; gr
           +ounder merges them into `attributes`. ¬ß4.1.5 ‚ÄĒ attribute matc
           +hing fallback also checks object `name` for the descriptor wo
           +rd.                                                          
      1610 +                                                             
      1611 +#### 13.12.3 Boundary Clearance Inconsistency                
      1612 +                                                             
      1613 +**Observed:** Screws removal ‚ÄĒ `goal_error=120.6` for the bes
           +t trajectory, meaning the trajectory endpoint is 120px from t
           +he boundary target. The generator clamps at 5px but the rollo
           +ut border collision uses 10px, creating an inconsistency wher
           +e trajectories near the edge that were valid at generation ti
           +me register as collisions at simulation time.                
      1614 +                                                             
      1615 +**Fix:** Unified `BOUNDARY_CLEARANCE = 5` constant (¬ß4.4.2, ¬ß
           +4.7, ¬ß6). Both generation clamp and rollout border margin use
           + the same value. Removal trajectories aim for `BOUNDARY_CLEAR
           +ANCE` pixels from the edge, not 0px, ensuring they are genuin
           +ely reachable without collision.

‚óŹ SPEC.md is updated. Here's what was captured and where:

  ¬ß4.1.1a ‚ÄĒ VLM Grounding Prompt Requirements (new)
  Specifies that the VLM grounding prompt must request color, size, attributes
  per object. Grounder merges color/size into the attributes list. Enables
  downstream descriptor matching to work for "blue pliers", "big remote", "pink 
  pliers".

  ¬ß4.1.3 ‚ÄĒ Grounding Resolver (updated)
  Resolution step 1 now specifies synonym-tolerant matching: exact word ‚Üí
  substring ‚Üí synonym expansion. "remote" matches "TV remote", "apple" matches
  "peach" via synonym table.

  ¬ß4.1.4 ‚ÄĒ Object Name Matching and Synonym Expansion (new)
  Canonical spec for the three-tier match (word ‚Üí substring ‚Üí synonym). Synonym
  table for common aliases (apple/fruit, remote/controller, glass/cup, etc.).
  OBJECT_SYNONYMS dict in config for extension.

  ¬ß4.1.5 ‚ÄĒ Attribute-Based Object Selection (new)
  Specifies that attribute descriptors (color, size) are matched against
  attributes list, object name words, and spatial_description. Fallback chain if
  attribute over-constrains ‚Üí ignore filter.

  ¬ß4.4.2 ‚ÄĒ Trajectory Generation (updated)
  BOUNDARY_CLEARANCE = 5px named as the single authoritative constant for
  waypoint clamping, replacing the hardcoded 5.

  ¬ß4.7 ‚ÄĒ Rollout border margin (updated)
  Border collision now references BOUNDARY_CLEARANCE (5px), not the previous
  hardcoded 10px. Both generation and simulation use the same constant.

  ¬ß6 ‚ÄĒ Config (updated)
  BOUNDARY_CLEARANCE = 5 and OBJECT_SYNONYMS dict added.

  ¬ß13.12 ‚ÄĒ Trace Analysis Findings (new)
  Three subsections documenting each issue: grounding name mismatch,
  attribute-based disambiguation failure, boundary clearance inconsistency ‚ÄĒ
  each with root cause, fix reference, and prerequisite implementation tracking
  table.

‚óŹ The images make the problem clear. For screws ‚ÄĒ the bboxes are tall rectangles
  starting from near the top of the image because the VLM is estimating the
  full shank length, not a tight box. For apples ‚ÄĒ the boxes are shifted above
  the actual fruits. Both are VLM bbox offset issues.

  The core fix: the VLM prompt needs to request tight bboxes AND an explicit
  center pixel. Currently we compute the center from the bbox midpoint, which
  inherits the offset. If the VLM gives us a direct center pixel estimate it
  will be more accurate regardless of bbox quality.

  Let me run the current pipeline on both images to see what the latest code
  produces, then fix the prompt and center computation.

  Thought for 43s, ran 2 shell commands (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ The images confirm two distinct problems:

  Screws: VLM returns very tall narrow bboxes spanning the entire screw shank
  (y: 68‚Üí310 for a 40px wide screw). The bbox midpoint ends up mid-shank, not at
  the screw head. Trajectory starts from mid-shank instead of the visible head.

  Apples/peaches: Bboxes are shifted ‚ÄĒ the VLM estimated the fruit positions but
  with significant y-offset from the actual fruit centroids.

  The root cause: we derive center purely from (x1+x2)//2, (y1+y2)//2 of a loose
  VLM bbox. The fix is to ask the VLM to return an explicit center pixel (cx,
  cy) alongside the bbox ‚ÄĒ the VLM can localise the object center visually much
  more accurately than computing a midpoint from a loose rectangle.

‚óŹ The pixel sampling is conclusive ‚ÄĒ the peach centers at (270,845) and
  (420,840) are landing on white background (RGB ~173,180,173), not on orange
  fruit. The VLM bbox is shifted off the actual fruit regardless of what cx/cy
  it reports. The cx/cy are essentially just being computed as the bbox
  midpoint.

  The real fix: after getting VLM bboxes, refine the center using image analysis
  ‚ÄĒ find the centroid of the high-gradient (object boundary) pixels within the
  bbox. Objects have edges; white table background is smooth. This will pull the
  center onto the actual object regardless of VLM accuracy.

‚óŹ Now I'll add a _refine_center function that uses image content within the VLM
  bbox to find the actual object centroid:

‚óŹ Update(pivot\vlm\grounder.py)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 61 lines
      148      return f"{label} {name}"
      149  
      150  
      151 +def _refine_center_from_image(image, bbox, cx_hint, cy_hint): 
      152 +    """                                                       
      153 +    Refine the VLM-reported center to the actual pixel centroi
          +d of the object                                               
      154 +    within the bbox, using gradient magnitude to locate the ob
          +ject boundary.                                                
      155 +                                                              
      156 +    Strategy:                                                 
      157 +      1. Expand the search region 20% around the VLM bbox to c
          +atch objects                                                  
      158 +         that overflow the bbox.                              
      159 +      2. Compute gradient magnitude (Sobel) ‚ÄĒ high gradient = 
          +object boundary.                                              
      160 +      3. Threshold to a foreground mask (top-30% gradient pixe
          +ls).                                                          
      161 +      4. Compute the centroid of the foreground mask.         
      162 +      5. If the centroid moves more than half the bbox size fr
          +om the hint,                                                  
      163 +         fall back to the hint (prevents jumping to a differen
          +t object).                                                    
      164 +                                                              
      165 +    Returns (cx, cy) refined pixel center.                    
      166 +    """                                                       
      167 +    h, w = image.shape[:2]                                    
      168 +    x1, y1, x2, y2 = bbox                                     
      169 +                                                              
      170 +    # Expand region by 20%                                    
      171 +    pad_x = max(int((x2 - x1) * 0.20), 10)                    
      172 +    pad_y = max(int((y2 - y1) * 0.20), 10)                    
      173 +    rx1 = max(x1 - pad_x, 0)                                  
      174 +    ry1 = max(y1 - pad_y, 0)                                  
      175 +    rx2 = min(x2 + pad_x, w - 1)                              
      176 +    ry2 = min(y2 + pad_y, h - 1)                              
      177 +                                                              
      178 +    if rx2 <= rx1 or ry2 <= ry1:                              
      179 +        return cx_hint, cy_hint                               
      180 +                                                              
      181 +    region = image[ry1:ry2, rx1:rx2]                          
      182 +    if region.size == 0:                                      
      183 +        return cx_hint, cy_hint                               
      184 +                                                              
      185 +    gray = cv2.cvtColor(region, cv2.COLOR_BGR2GRAY) if region.
          +ndim == 3 else region                                         
      186 +    gx = cv2.Sobel(gray, cv2.CV_32F, 1, 0, ksize=3)           
      187 +    gy = cv2.Sobel(gray, cv2.CV_32F, 0, 1, ksize=3)           
      188 +    grad = np.sqrt(gx**2 + gy**2)                             
      189 +                                                              
      190 +    # Also include pixels that differ significantly from backg
          +round (edges of image)                                        
      191 +    # Threshold: top 30% of gradient values                   
      192 +    thresh = np.percentile(grad, 70)                          
      193 +    mask = (grad >= thresh).astype(np.float32)                
      194 +                                                              
      195 +    total = mask.sum()                                        
      196 +    if total < 10:                                            
      197 +        return cx_hint, cy_hint                               
      198 +                                                              
      199 +    ys, xs = np.where(mask > 0)                               
      200 +    refined_cx = int(xs.mean()) + rx1                         
      201 +    refined_cy = int(ys.mean()) + ry1                         
      202 +                                                              
      203 +    # Sanity check: don't move more than half the bbox width/h
          +eight from hint                                               
      204 +    max_drift_x = max((x2 - x1) // 2, 20)                     
      205 +    max_drift_y = max((y2 - y1) // 2, 20)                     
      206 +    if abs(refined_cx - cx_hint) > max_drift_x or abs(refined_
          +cy - cy_hint) > max_drift_y:                                  
      207 +        return cx_hint, cy_hint                               
      208 +                                                              
      209 +    return _clamp(refined_cx, 0, w - 1), _clamp(refined_cy, 0,
          + h - 1)                                                       
      210 +                                                              
      211 +                                                              
      212  def _assign_ids_and_descriptions(objects):
      213      """
      214      Add object_id, attributes, spatial_description to each obj
           ect in-place.

‚óŹ The gradient approach isn't working for the apple case ‚ÄĒ (250,831) is still on
  white/grey background (RGB 221,227,234). The problem is the background IS
  high-gradient too because the table edge, laptop screen, and other items
  create gradients everywhere. Gradient-based refinement is wrong for cluttered
  scenes.

  The correct approach for the apple/peach case: the VLM bbox itself is offset ‚ÄĒ
  [220,780,340,890] is positioned above the actual fruit. We need to find the
  most visually distinct region within the bbox compared to the surrounding area
  ‚ÄĒ that's the object. The right technique is to look for the dominant
  non-background color cluster inside the bbox.

  Let me look at what pixel values are actually at the fruit locations:

  Ran 2 shell commands (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Now I see the real problem. The fruit is at y=1040‚Äď1175 (centroid y‚Čą1107), but
  the VLM bbox says [220,780,340,890] ‚ÄĒ it's off by ~250px in Y. The processing
  image is 853√ó1280 and the fruits are in the bottom quarter of the image. The
  VLM is reporting coordinates that are significantly above the actual object
  positions.

  This is a VLM coordinate system mismatch ‚ÄĒ the VLM likely sees a downscaled
  thumbnail and returns coordinates in thumbnail space rather than the 853√ó1280
  processing space. Let me check the actual vs expected scale:

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)
‚óŹ The ratio 830/1107 = 0.75 and 960/1280 = 0.75 match exactly. The VLM is 
  internally downscaling the image to a 960px max dimension before processing,
  but returning coordinates in that downscaled space. We send it 853√ó1280 but it
  reasons about it as 640√ó960.

  The fix: after getting VLM coordinates, scale them up by 1280/960 = 4/3 to
  convert back to our processing image space. Let me verify this hypothesis:

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

  screws look like. The correction works perfectly for screws. The peaches still

‚óŹ The corrected center (360,1113) is right on the left edge of the left peach ‚ÄĒ
  the * pixels (warm/orange) are at (360,1073) through (345,1158). The actual
  fruit centroid is slightly to the upper-left of our corrected position. The
  correction is working ‚ÄĒ we just need to use the cluster centroid rather than
  the exact corrected point.

  The key insight confirmed: the VLM is using a 960px max-dimension internal 
  scale. The fix is to detect this scale factor and apply it to all returned
  coordinates. The factor is max(image_h, image_w) / 960 when max(h,w) > 960,
  else 1.0.

          +this factor.

      169  def _refine_center_from_image(image, bbox, cx_hint, cy_hint):
      170      """
      171 -    Refine the VLM-reported center to the actual pixel centroi
          -d of the object                                               
      172 -    within the bbox, using gradient magnitude to locate the ob
          -ject boundary.                                                
      171 +    Refine the VLM-reported (scale-corrected) center to the ac
          +tual pixel                                                    
      172 +    centroid of the object within the bbox.                   
      173  
      174 -    Strategy:                                                 
      175 -      1. Expand the search region 20% around the VLM bbox to c
          -atch objects                                                  
      176 -         that overflow the bbox.                              
      177 -      2. Compute gradient magnitude (Sobel) ‚ÄĒ high gradient = 
          -object boundary.                                              
      178 -      3. Threshold to a foreground mask (top-30% gradient pixe
          -ls).                                                          
      179 -      4. Compute the centroid of the foreground mask.         
      180 -      5. If the centroid moves more than half the bbox size fr
          -om the hint,                                                  
      181 -         fall back to the hint (prevents jumping to a differen
          -t object).                                                    
      174 +    Strategy ‚ÄĒ find the dominant non-background cluster:      
      175 +      1. Expand the search region 30% around the scaled VLM bb
          +ox.                                                           
      176 +      2. Compute local color variance ‚ÄĒ background (plain tabl
          +e/wall) is                                                    
      177 +         low-variance; objects are higher-variance or distinct
          +ly colored.                                                   
      178 +      3. Also build a saturation mask ‚ÄĒ objects tend to be mor
          +e saturated                                                   
      179 +         than white/grey backgrounds.                         
      180 +      4. Weight pixels by max(local_variance, saturation) and 
          +compute                                                       
      181 +         weighted centroid.                                   
      182 +      5. Sanity-check: don't drift more than one bbox-size fro
          +m hint.                                                       
      183

  Committed c605fd5, ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Committed as c605fd5. The two-layer fix:

  1. Coordinate scale correction ‚ÄĒ Claude Vision downsizes images to 960px max
  before processing but returns coordinates in that space. A 1280px-tall image
  was getting VLM coordinates that were off by 1.333√ó (1280/960). Every bbox and
  center pixel is now multiplied by _vlm_coord_scale() immediately after
  parsing the VLM response.

  2. Saturation-weighted centroid refinement ‚ÄĒ after scale correction the bbox
  region is now in roughly the right area, but the exact center may still fall
  on background (table/wall are low-saturation grey/white). The refinement
  computes a weighted centroid within the expanded bbox where the weight is
  saturation + 2√ólocal_variance ‚ÄĒ objects are more saturated and more textured
  than plain backgrounds, so the centroid is pulled onto the actual object.

      119 +def _parse_workspace_anchor(text, image_shape):               
      120 +    """                                                       
      121 +    If text contains a spatial anchor phrase, return the corre
          +sponding (gx, gy)                                             
      122 +    in image pixel coordinates.  Returns None if no anchor phr
          +ase found.                                                    
      123 +    """                                                       
      124 +    if not text:                                              
      125 +        return None                                           
      126 +    h, w = image_shape[:2]                                    
      127 +    bc = BOUNDARY_CLEARANCE                                   
      128 +    for pattern, (fx, fy) in _ANCHOR_PATTERNS:                
      129 +        if pattern.search(text):                              
      130 +            gx = int(np.clip(fx * w, bc, w - bc))             
      131 +            gy = int(np.clip(fy * h, bc, h - bc))             
      132 +            return (gx, gy)                                   
      133 +    return None                                               
      134 +                                                              
      135 +

‚óŹ Committed as e4ce30b. Summary of what was done and why:

  Blue square not detected in img_13 ‚ÄĒ two bugs:

  1. HSV range too narrow: The blue square has H=99‚Äď102, right at the lower
  bound of H=100. Widened to H=90 so the full range of blue-teal colours is
  captured. Also lowered S/V minimums slightly (80,60) for robustness.
  2. _MIN_BLOCK_AREA=400 too aggressive: The contour algorithm gives area=361
  for these synthetic squares (contour approximation underestimates slightly vs.
  bounding box area). Lowered to 300 ‚ÄĒ still large enough to reject JPEG noise
  (which produces sub-50px¬≤ blobs) but captures the actual squares.

  Workspace anchor goal mapping ("middle of surface", "top left corner" etc.):

  - Added _ANCHOR_PATTERNS table mapping 15+ natural-language spatial anchor
  phrases to image-fraction coordinates (fx, fy)
  - _compute_goal_pixel checks anchors first ‚ÄĒ before
  distance/direction/relation logic
  - check_interrupt suppresses GOAL_UNMAPPABLE and
  INSUFFICIENT_GOAL_SPECIFICATION when an anchor is present ‚ÄĒ the anchor
  provides a complete goal even when direction=None or goal_complete=False
  - SPEC.md ¬ß4.4.1 updated with full anchor table and example prompts

          -LM payload < 5MB), tracks `(scale_x, scale_y)`,

          -ates for final output via `scale_objects()`.                  
       60 -All pipeline internals (trajectories, goal_pixel, bboxes) oper
          -ate in **downscaled space**.                                  
       78 +`main.py` downscales images with long edge > 1280px, tracks `(
          +scale_x, scale_y)`. All pipeline                              
       79 +internals operate in downscaled space. Final outputs are resca
          +led to original resolution.

       91  
       74 -## Goal completeness model                                    
       75 -- `underspecified` (direction only, no distance/reference) ‚Üí r
          -aises `INSUFFICIENT_GOAL_SPECIFICATION` interrupt             
       76 -- `explicit` (e.g. "100 pixels left", "to x=150") ‚Üí trajectory
          - length equals stated distance                                
       77 -- `image_derivable` (e.g. "left of blue square") ‚Üí goal pixel 
          -derived from reference object center                          
       92 +## Goal resolution model                                      
       93  
       79 -Goal interpretation has two paths: offline regex (`_parse_offl
          -ine`) and VLM (`_parse_vlm`). VLM path                        
       80 -is used only when `USE_VLM=True`; offline path handles motion/
          -placement/removal/containment/state_change.                   
       94 +**Workspace anchor phrases** (resolved in `_compute_goal_pixel
          +` before all other logic):                                    
       95 +- `"middle of surface"`, `"centre of table"` ‚Üí image center (5
          +0%, 50%)                                                      
       96 +- `"top left corner"` ‚Üí (10%, 10%); `"top right corner"` ‚Üí (90
          +%, 10%)                                                       
       97 +- `"leftmost"`, `"left most end"`, `"far left"` ‚Üí (5%, 50%)   
       98 +- `"top"`, `"top of table"` ‚Üí (50%, 10%); `"bottom"` ‚Üí (50%, 9
          +0%)                                                           
       99 +- When an anchor is matched: `GOAL_UNMAPPABLE` and `INSUFFICIE
          +NT_GOAL_SPECIFICATION` are suppressed

      101 +**movement_specification values:**                            
      102 +- `underspecified` ‚Üí raises `INSUFFICIENT_GOAL_SPECIFICATION` 
          +(unless anchor present)                                       
      103 +- `explicit` (e.g. "100 pixels left", "to x=150") ‚Üí trajectory
          + length equals stated distance                                
      104 +- `image_derivable` (e.g. "left of blue square") ‚Üí goal pixel 
          +from reference object center

          -easoning`, `simulation_results`,

      106 +**Removal goals:** any reference to a surface/region (`table`,
          + `shelf`, `background`, etc.) after "from" is treated as a sou
          +rce region ‚ÄĒ not required to be grounded. Pipeline logs a warn
          +ing and continues, routing the trajectory to the nearest image
          + boundary.

      108 +**Multi-object auto-selection (¬ß4.4.6):** when `quantity_expli
          +cit=True` (e.g. "remove one screw") and multiple matching obje
          +cts exist, the pipeline evaluates trajectories for all candida
          +tes and selects the best by planning cost instead of interrupt
          +ing.

      153 +## Known VLM grounding behaviour                              
      154 +- Claude Vision uses 960px max internal resolution ‚ÄĒ all retur
          +ned coordinates are multiplied by `max(h,w)/960` to convert ba
          +ck to processing image space                                  
      155 +- VLM names may differ from prompt nouns ‚ÄĒ `OBJECT_SYNONYMS` i
          +n `config.py` handles common aliases                          
      156 +- For JPEG real-world images, HSV grounding is disabled (JPEG 
          +compression creates false blobs)
